it be the fragment "b"?

John

Date:  Mon, 17 Jan 2011 22:53:44 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  C/2010B1 (Cardinal) image
Hi,

please find attached to this email an image that I took of C/2010B1 last night (2011 Jan 16.5 UT) through a 35cm ACF SCT with STL11000M CCD. I Sum stacked 12 x 2min clear images @ 2x2 @-20c.

Note the tail extending for about 6’ in a PA of ~300*. North = up and east = left. The image has been cropped to roughly 15’ x 12’.

Cheers

John Drummond

Date:  Sat, 29 Jan 2011 12:09:12 -0000
From:  Martin Gembec 
Subject:  103P near Seagull nebula
Hi!

Finally clouds are gone. Cold (-6°C) and dry (65%) air, good conditions for imaging, even in the boundary of city (40 thousand people).

Comet is clearly visible near IC 2177 (Seagull nebula). I used my Celestron ED 80/600 (with 0,67x Vixen reducer) and Canon 30Dmod with CLS filter. Guided on GSO mount with 70/500 refractor and autoguider. I put 6x5min images near the center of coma into an image of 20x5min, ISO 800 (nebula and comet), because some movement in longer exposures was visible.

Info and image here:
http://udalosti.astronomy.cz/?p=211

Martin Gembec, Czech Republic. 

Date:  Sat, 29 Jan 2011 13:25:57 +0100
From:  ligustri rolando 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 103P near Seagull nebula
great picture! :-)))

regards
Rolando

Date:  Mon, 31 Jan 2011 23:00:49 +1100
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  comet 2010 X1 Elenin image Jan 28 2011
Hi all,

Find a recent image of comet 2010 x1 Elenin om my website.
http://members.westnet.com.au/mmatti/sc.htm
and click on comet Elenin link.
It's pretty faint at around magnitude 17.5.
This would put its absolute magnitude at 9.5-10 and suggest a peak of only
magnitude 5 in September.
However, still early days!

cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo

Date:  Tue, 05 Apr 2011 09:35:11 -0000
From:  Soulier J-FranÃ§ois 
Subject:  C 2011 A3 Gibbs ?

Hello everyone.

I'd like to know whether professionals or amateurs had recently observed
C 2011 A3 Gibbs, and would have detected a condensation (fragmentation)
secondary to the main kernel ?
I have pictures of it dated 20110324 and 20110402, which shows an object
in the following positions :

NET USNO-B1.0
JF24c03 KC2011 03 24.98779 13 36 26.31 +24 39 47.3 20.4 R
C10
JF24c03 KC2011 03 25.00096 13 36 25.87 +24 39 52.4 20.6 R
C10
----- end -----
NET USNO-B1.0
JF02d01 KC2011 04 02.04521 13 32 54.57 +25 42 04.2 20.4 R
C10
JF02d01 KC2011 04 02.05724 13 32 54.31 +25 42 10.0 20.1 R
C10
----- end -----
Radius measurement : 4".
Sampling : 2.04"/pix.
Position in main core : +/- 12" and +/- 15".
The page on my observations :
http://6888comete.free.fr/fr/imageC2011A3gibbsfrance.htm


In advance, with many thanks.

Best regards to all the list.
SOULIER Jean-François
C10/France

Date:  Sat, 09 Apr 2011 13:48:46 +0200
From:  Bernd Häusler 
Subject:  documentation of the small outburst of 240P/NEAT
Hello all,

thanks to the numerous observations since the posting of the outburst in the
Yahoo groups and based on the last measurements recently published by
M.P.E.C. 2011-G58, I generated a light curve with COMET for Windows of
Seiichi Yoshida representing the actual outburst of 240P/NEAT.

Last image of April, 8 2011.
overview of comet 240P.

The outburst seams actually to stay on the level of 16 mag coming from
around 18 mag end of March and maybe visible for some of the experienced
observers here.

Hope everybody can follow the links in this email.
Clear skies and good luck
Bernhard Haeusler

B82 Maidbronn 

Date:  Sat, 09 Apr 2011 13:52:10 +0200
From:  Bernd Häusler 
Subject:  documentation of the outburst of 240P/NEAT with links
Hello all,

thanks to the numerous observations since the posting of the outburst in the
Yahoo groups and based on the last measurements recently published by
M.P.E.C. 2011-G58, I generated a light curve with COMET for Windows of
Seiichi Yoshida representing the actual outburst of 240P/NEAT:
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/240p.htm#a1

Last image of April, 8 2011:
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/240p_20110408.htm

overview of comet 240P:
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/240p.htm

The outburst seams actually to stay on the level of 16 mag coming from
around 18 mag end of March and maybe visible for some of the experienced
observers here.

Subject:  Images of some poorly observed comets
Hi all,

Recenty I remotely observed C/2006 W3, C/2007 Q3, C/2009 F4, C/2009 S3, P/2010 D2, C/2010 R1, C/2011 C3 and 213P.

C/2006 W3 (m1 = 16.4)
https://picasaweb.google.com/104133965506763777371/PICASA#5600540753741978162

C/2007 Q3 (m1 = 17.5, diffuse)
https://picasaweb.google.com/104133965506763777371/PICASA#5601989824618185282

C/2009 F4 (m1 = 13.4, very bright)

Comet C/2010 G2 (Hill)in Camelopards is currently about magnitude 14 and getting brighter. I imaged it last night under mag 5 skies and it was a real challenge for me. Date:  Tue, 31 May 2011 23:15:50 +1000
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  C/2010 X1 (Elenin) image May 31 2011
Hello all,

I have imaged Comet Elenin this evening.
It is not brighter than magnitude 14, and more likely about mag 15.0
see :
http://members.westnet.com.au/mmatti/sc.htm
My CCD camera is a one shot colour imager (starlight express) with sensitivity near the visual range.
You can see that mag 15 PGC galaxies are even more visible than the comet!

This is not good news for a bright performance.
If it continues , expect mag 6 at best, if it manages to survive perihelion in September.
On the other hand, gas comets brighten more rapidly on approach to perihelion.
Perhaps wait for a month and see :)
the current magnitude formula is m1 = 10.0 + 5 log d + 10.0 log r

cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo
Castlemaine Victoria

Date:  Thu, 02 Jun 2011 23:32:16 -0000
From:  dennis_persyk 
Subject:  C/2009 P1 Garradd -- Brightest comet in the Sky!
I got up at 2:30 am to image this comet in early morning twilight from my North-Central Illinois observatory. The best frames were taken at around 3:50. By then there was considerable morning twilight from the rising sun but the comet was also higher in the sky, away from the sky glow near the horizon. The function describing the optimum exposure as a function of increasing twilight and increasing comet elevation would be helpful to know. I'd appreciate inputs on this. I had to just play around with varying exposure times to keep the background sky glow from saturating, and it was a constantly-changing ordeal.

I know this comet isn't much to look at, but it is the best I can do right now . However, by February, 2012, this comet is forecast to be much brighter at magnitude 6. I will have to be patient.

For more details, visit my New Images web page
http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm

Images, commentary, data and all kinds of good info at the link below -- please take a look.

http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm .

Clear skies,

Dennis Persyk

Date:  Sun, 05 Jun 2011 00:07:49 +1000
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  Comet images June 4 2011
Hello all,

I have uploaded images of the following comets to my webpage:
C/2010 x1 Elenin
29P Schwassmann-Wachmann 1
174P Echeclus

http://members.westnet.com.au/mmatti/sc.htm

Comet Elenin is currently about magnitude 14 and may reach magnitude 6 in
September.
29P is having a bright outburst and displays a sharply curving dust fan.
Visual mag of 12.0
174P is a Centaur in outburst at mag 16, beyond the orbit of Jupiter.

cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo
Castlemaine Victoria

Hello all,

I have uploaded images of the following comets to my webpage:
Taken tonight June 28, 2011
C/2010 X1 Elenin
29P Schwassmann-Wachmann 1
C/2009 F4 McNaught

http://members.westnet.com.au/mmatti/sc.htm

29P displays a bright stellar nucleus of magnitude 12 - yet another
outburst!
2009 F4 is about magnitude 13, well condensed with nice tail.

Date:  Fri, 01 Jul 2011 10:13:57 -0500
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  ASO image of C/2009 P1 of 30 June 2011
Narrow field image of c/2009 P1 with the ASO 0.51m astrograph, 35 sec, showing indication
of two tail extensions toward PA 169 to 238 deg.
The comet is exhibiting very fine development and our CCD estimate for total mag. was 10.3
at f/4.9 binned 2 x 2.
http://www.arksky.org/php/cdata.php?object=c2009xxxP1xxx(Garrard)
Complete comet update tables at:
http://www.arksky.org/php/ctable.php

Clay
_____
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
MPC H45 - Petit Jean Mountain South
MPC H41 - Petit Jean Mountain
MPC H43 - Conway West
http://www.arksky.org/

Date:  Sun, 03 Jul 2011 10:52:18 +0200
From:  Erik Bryssinck 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] image of C/2009 P1 of 30 June 2011 (color)


Hi John,

The telescope is a Epsilon 180mm Corrected Newtonian combined with an SBIG one-shot color camera (ST-2000). It features a very fast speed (f/2.8) using an ED (Extra-low Dispersion)corrector. The image is a single shot of 600 sec. exposuretime.

best regards,

Erik

Subject:  are slooh pics allowed
I spent some time figuring out how to use slooh.com in conjuction with the Earth Centered Universe and got my first comet pic via this new method.

Is that accepted here, or frowned upon? I do not have super equipment, got back problems, which make hauling out the scopes I have a bit more difficult than it used to be and basically resort to only doing visual observations so now and then (got a busy life so that doesn't help either, but who doesn't).

let me know and I will post my first slooh comet pic here of Garradd.

Ellen - SW Ontario

Date:  Thu, 21 Jul 2011 21:59:24 +1000
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  comet images July 21 2011: C/2010 X1  29P
Hello all,

I have uploaded images of the following comets to my webpage taken July 21,
2011

C/2010 X1 Elenin
29P Schwassmann-Wachmann 1

http://members.westnet.com.au/mmatti/sc.htm

Comet Elenin is now visually observable at magnitude 10.5, displaying a
moderately condensed coma 3' wide
through a 20cm reflector at 45x. The coma is enhanced with a swan band
filter.
This is my first visual observation and I should be able to follow it into
perihelion in mid September when it may be as bright as mag 4.

29P has now diffused out after its outburst last month but still displays a
bright dusty asymmetric coma.

cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo
Castlemaine Victoria

Subject:  P/Honda-Mrkos-Pajdusakova-45P imaged last night
Hi,

I imaged P/Honda-Mrkos-Pajdusakova-45P last night (2011 July 26.6 UT) with the 35cm f10 Meade ACF SCT and SBIG STL11000M CCD. I took 1 minute sub-lights – 6 x clear, 3 x rgb. –25c. I know it’s a rubbish image but some may find it of interest.

I also used the Clear images for astrometry -

----- Original Message -----
From: "P. Clay Sherrod"
To:
Sent: Wednesday, July 27, 2011 2:04 AM
Subject: Fragment in comet 45P

> Suspected on July 26 (U.T.) and confirmed this morning (July 27 U.T.) is a fairly large
> (~mag. 17.2) fragment located 6.8" in P.A. 127 deg from the main nucleus of comet 45P
> Honda-Mrkos-Padjusakova.
>
> The comet's appearance via 45-sec CCD is quite irregular throughout the length of the
> tail (tadpole-shaped) with a "lump" evident at the position of this secondary fragment.
> High resolution imaging near the nucleus reveals the secondary fragment, which is nearly
> in line with the irregular tail, itself angled at 130 degrees. Posted currently on my
> website at
> http://www.arksky.org/php/cdata_admin.php?object=45Pxxx(Honda-Mrkos-Pajdusakova)
> is the wide field ( 22 x 15') view of the irregular shape of the comet and a high
> resolution image showing the faint fragment is being processed and will be posted at
> that same link later today.
>
> Astrometry of 45P from H45 (Petit Jean Mountain South) is as follows:
> (0.51m ASO astrograph @ f/4.9 + CCD, 2x2 binned)
>
> 0045P C2011 07 27.27230 21 56 18.32 -25 26 53.3 15.8 T H45
> 0045P C2011 07 27.27344 21 56 18.39 -25 26 55.7 15.9 T H45
> 0045P C2011 07 27.27535 21 56 18.49 -25 27 00.0 15.8 T H45
> 0045P C2011 07 27.27969 21 56 18.76 -25 27 09.9 15.7 T H45
> 0045P C2011 07 27.28131 21 56 18.84 -25 27 13.5 15.7 T H45
> 0045P C2011 07 27.28295 21 56 18.95 -25 27 17.3 15.7 T H45
> 0045P C2011 07 27.28476 21 56 19.05 -25 27 21.4 15.7 T H45
> ______________
> Clearly this is an unusual and active comet at this time and bears watching by observers
> in the southern hemisphere. It is getting far too low from here in Arkansas.
>
> Clay

> Dr. P. Clay Sherrod

> MPC H45 Petit Jean Mountain South

Date:  Sat, 30 Jul 2011 12:32:41 +1200
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  C/2010 X1 (Elenin) from last night
Hi,

I imaged C/2010 X1 (Elenin) last night with the 35cm (14”) Meade ACF SCT at f10. I used the SBIG STL11000M CCD and just took images through the Clear filter. The exposures were three minutes each and I combined eight of them. The time was 2011 July 29.25 – .29. The image has been cropped so that it’s about 15’ x 10’. North is up, East is left.

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory Complex
International Astro Union Code: E94
Gisborne, New Zealand
E: 177d 53', S: 38d 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm
Phone (mobile): 0275 609 287

Date:  Mon, 01 Aug 2011 21:52:11 -0000
From:  astrogeek_andre 
Subject:  Another C2009/P1 (Garradd)
Hi Folks,

Here is another shot of C2009/P1 (Garradd)

http://www.flickr.com/photos/26671216@N02/5999720762
Click on the '+' button near the top to get access to other resolutions.

The image data was processed twice: once on the stars (to reject the moving comet) and once on the comet (to reject the stars). The two images were overlaid in Photoshop so that the detail around the comet could be seen in addition to the fainter parts of the comet tail. There are still remnant of the star trails visible in the image, giving it a sense of motion.

A pleasing blue planetary nebula (NGC 7094) can be found in the upper-left corner.

Cheers,

Andre

Date:  Fri, 05 Aug 2011 17:40:00 +0200
From:  "gvnn64\@libero\.it" 
Subject:  Image of 213P/Van Ness and its possible fragment
Hi,
at this link you can find our stacked image of comet 213P/Van Ness, and its possible fragment (the latter is placed about 5.3 arcmin in PA 239 with respect the main central condensation of the comet): http://tinyurl.com/3u3ylbg

Comet 213P shows also an obvious anti-tail, or dust-trail, at least 6-arcmin long in PA 58. Our rendition of this feature, obtained during the same observing session, is visible here: http://tinyurl.com/3qjlegz

With kind regards,
Giovanni Sostero, Nick Howes, Helen Blyth and Ernesto Guido

From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Image of 213P/Van Ness and its possible fragment
I would say that there is no doubt this is a fragment based on the apparent motion and the
angle of its own tail in concert with that of the fragment; tonight is clear here (so it
appears thus far and we will be able to get an image of it around 06:00 UT).

Excellent work on this and a very fine representation of this fragment.

Clay

Dr. P. Clay Sherrod

> at the time of Francois imaging.

Date:  Sun, 14 Aug 2011 17:44:05 -0000
From:  Rob 
Subject:  Comet 45P/Honda-Mrkos-Pajdusakova, 14 Aug 2011
Hard to pin down, moving so fast at just under a degree/two hours now. Add to that very bright moonlight, a light haze and a comet not much brighter than mag 10. Stack of 9 x 35-sec subs, piggybacked Canon 400D at 200mm.

Date:  Wed, 17 Aug 2011 14:01:52 -0000
From:  Piotr Malinski 
Subject:  C/2009 P1 Garradd from 14.08.2011
I've managed to capture C/2009 P1 Garradd last weekend. Moon was up, but that didn't stopped the imaging. I've used DSI III Pro and for tests - f/3.3 reducer with C11 at shorter distance (~40 mm for lesser reduction) to see how it would work with DSI... (It did awful, but the comet was visible...)

First "channel" was UHC-S (as ALP filter) and that gave good results (~50 x 30 sec + ~16 x 60 sec; 20:21 - 21:14 UT):
http://www.rkastrofoto.appspot.com/site_media/astro/orig/garrad-14-08-2011/comet0.jpg
http://www.rkastrofoto.appspot.com/site_media/astro/thumb/garrad-14-08-2011/comet1.jpg
http://www.rkastrofoto.appspot.com/site_media/astro/thumb/garrad-14-08-2011/comet2.jpg

And animation using 60 sec frames: http://www.rkastrofoto.appspot.com/site_media/astro/orig/garrad-14-08-2011/anim.gif

Second one was a test - Wratten #47 and Schott BG39 (uv/blue) to catch emission in CN and C3 bands (http://astrosurf.com/buil/garradd/obs.htm) - that didn't worked well as the background was very strong and I had some halos/reflections. I got the comet core and nothing more (except noise).

Date:  Fri, 19 Aug 2011 23:47:27 +1000
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  Comet images August 19 2011: C/2010 X1 Elenin C/2009 P1 Garradd
Hello all,

I have uploaded images of the following comets to my webpage taken August
19, 2011

C/2010 X1 Elenin
C/2009 P1 Garradd

http://members.westnet.com.au/mmatti/sc.htm

C/2010 X1 is visually observable at magnitude 8.1, displaying a
moderately condensed coma 4' wide through 4" binoculars.

C/2009 P1 is visually observable at magnitude 7.8 displaying a
strongly condensed coma 6' wide through 4" binoculars.

cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo

Hi,

I've just imaged the area of SQ6E1D7 and yes, it looks like quite a bright
comet. The image is attached - as is some astrometry I did (20 minutes)
before the cloud rolled in - and before I could get a visual observation
done. It will probably clear later.

At a VERY ROUGH mag guestimate based on images I would say it's about M1 =
14.5.

Congats to Rob or Gordon...

From:  SabiaJohn@aol.com
Subject:  Image of C/2009 P1 on August 23, 2011 UT
I placed a photo of this comet in the files section today.

Images with a STL1001E on a RCOptics RC20 f/8.1. A V filter was used for the 3, 60 second stacked images.

I was able to see this comet with 9 x 30 binoculars later when it was near zenith. Very diffuse object below Gamma Sagittae. My first view of this comet in darkskies.

John D Sabia

Date:  Sat, 03 Sep 2011 00:55:48 -0000
From:  dennis_persyk 
Subject:  C/2009 P1 Garradd
The last time I imaged this comet -- actually, the last time I imaged anything in the sky, was way back on June 1st. At that time the comet was a tiny blob at magnitude 11.1. Tonight it was magnitude 8.2 The magnitude difference of 2.9 corresponds to a brightness difference of 14.5.

For more details, visit my New Images web page
http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm

Images, commentary, data and all kinds of good info at the link below -- please take a look.

http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm .

Clear skies,

Dennis Persyk
Hampshire, IL
Igloo (Now Roll-Off) Observatory Home Page http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk
New Images http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm
Pier Design http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/Pier_Design.htm
Daily Bread Inspirational Page http://users.foxvalley.net/~dpersyk/DailyBread/

From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet Elenin imaged last night
Hi,

please find attached an image of Comet Elenin (C/2010 X1) taken last night (2011 September 03.29 (Saturday) UT) as it was setting in the moonlit sky. Even though it’s apparently disintegrating it still seems to have a fairly spherical head (in my humble opinion)...

35cm Meade ACF LX200 SCT, SBIG STL11000M CCD. 8 x 1 minute through the Clear filter (1x1).

Hi,

I imaged the new SWAN comet (with the designation of MATSON on the IAUMPC page) with the 35cm Meade SCT and SBIG STL11000M CCD about an hour ago (2011 Sept 05.32). I took two minute exposures. 10 x clear (1x1), 7 x RGB (3x3).

Astrometry taken from the images is below...

COD E94
CON John Drummond, 23 Bilham Road, Patutahi, Gisborne [john_drummond@xtra.co.nz]

Date:  Sat, 10 Sep 2011 17:01:22 -0000
From:  dennis_persyk 
Subject:  Comet C/2009 P1: Cooled CCD and DSLR
I have been learning how to take astrophotos with my Canon T1i DSLR. A few nights ago I imaged comet Garradd with both cooled CCD and DSLR at the same time.

The cooled ccd is an SXVR-H9 and the scope a 6-inch Takahashi E-160 f/3.3 astrograph. The DSLR the Canon T1i at ISO 400 on a 4-inch Teleview NP-101, f/5.4.

The cooled CCD camera has two advantages over the DSLR. Firstly, it was binned 2x2, affording 4 times the sensitivity. Secondly it is on a faster scope, yielding an increase in brightness of [(5.4/3.3) squared] = 2.7 .

In spite of the large differences , the DSLR performed admirably. Check it out for yourself at my New Images web page
http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm

I still have a lot to learn about optimum ISO, exposure times (although comet imaging time is limited by the comet's relative motion) and white balance parameters -- I'd appreciate advice on improving my images.

Clear skies,

Dennis Persyk
Hampshire, IL
Igloo (Now Roll-Off) Observatory Home Page http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk
New Images http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm
Pier Design http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/Pier_Design.htm
Daily Bread Inspirational Page http://users.foxvalley.net/~dpersyk/DailyBread/

Date:  Thu, 22 Sep 2011 15:31:41 -0000
From:  tricks46 
Subject:  New Scope
Hello all. Thought I would post her an image of a new scope I received a couple of days ago. This is new for me and will take a sharp learning curve as I have used refractor scopes for years. In the late 90's I used a 10" F 6.3 1600mm from Meade which is no longer produced. The TV127is is 660mm and I wanted to get more power but not that much so this xcope a Tak. CCA 250 is native 1250mm @ F 5. Not sure the mount will cary the load and if so it will max out. Hope to have it in service within a couple of months so wish me luck because I don't learn like I use to. Thanks for looking.
Mike H.
http://fototime.com/F2B8CD48642CCDD/orig.jpg

Date:  Mon, 26 Sep 2011 13:12:42 -0000
From:  Carey 
Subject:  Comet Garradd
I downloaded the orbits for the comets into Earth Centered Universe today before taking a group of people out for an astronomy tour. During the tour I took some quick shots of Comet Garradd. Now I'm home and looking at the images, and I couldn't get the starfield in the image and the program to match up. Then I noticed the comet I was looking at in ECU was 2008 P1 Garradd. Wait, what?! Went back to the list I downloaded today, sure enough there is a 2008 P1 Garradd & a 2009 P1 Garradd. 2008 P1 shows to be between Ursa Major & Ursa Minor.

Here is my image of 2009 P1.

http://www.flickr.com/photos/quarkcsj/6184688729/in/set-72157627631859061/lightbox/

Carey Johnson
Honolulu, HI

Date:  Mon, 26 Sep 2011 17:37:43 -0000
From:  Martin Gembec 
Subject:  45P image September 26th
Hi all, I tok some minute exposures in twilight of 45P/Honda-Mrkos-Pajdusakova. Visualy and also photographicaly nice comet. But my optics isn't so fast, so only hint of tail is visible, but about one degree from coma I think nice V shape of tail is good to recognize on negative version. From coma to the edge of image about 2 degrees.

Canon 30Dmod+ Celestron ED80/600 + Vixen 0.67x reducer. 16x1min, ISO800. Around 3:20 UTC.

http://udalosti.astronomy.cz/obraz/foto/comet/45p/45p-20110926-inv-cely.jpg

http://udalosti.astronomy.cz/obraz/foto/comet/45p/45p-20110926-svitani.jpg

Martin Gembec, Czech Republic

Date:  Fri, 30 Sep 2011 12:31:45 +1000
From:  Alan Watson 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Comet 45P in STEREO A
Gidday Carey,
Appart from Earth...
FOV range limit approx 11Mag
Asteroid - Vesta 3.07au from STEREOA approx 7.5 mag
Comet - 45P 0.8au from STEREOA approx 7.5 mag
Star - Deneb Algiedi approx 2.8 mag
Star - Nashira approx 3.65 mag
45P will brighten and get as close as approx 0.18 au.

Kind regards, Alan

Date:  Fri, 30 Sep 2011 16:07:49 +0200
From:  Bernd Häusler 
Subject:  don't omit 36P/Whipple these days
Hello collegues,

the comet reached its best window of observation this opposition.
Whipple's distance to Earth is actually 2.1 AU.
On my images the comet has a nice tail of 21.5" in PA 261°, the coma is
11.5", 17.8 mag (10x10). (Similiar also on Gerke's and Novichonok's image of
August, 28 found on Seiichi Yoshida's website).

Images and analysis of September, 30 2011 on:
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/36p_20110930.htm

overview:
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/36p.htm

Best Regards
Bernhard Haeusler
B82 Maidbronn
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/index.htm

Date:  Sun, 02 Oct 2011 18:09:59 -0000
From:  dennis_persyk 
Subject:  C/2009 P1 Reprocessed with Superimposed Head/Star Field
I have been learning how to take astrophotos with my Canon T1i DSLR. My first effort was posted a few weeks ago. I reprocessed it superimposing just the comet head on the background star field. This is my first attempt at this technique, so please be gentle in your criticisms.

Technique using ImagesPlus
Image 1: One hours' worth of subs aligned on comet; no stars because I used a median combine.
Image 2: A single sub with both head and stars sharply displayed.

I used Special Functions/Combine Images and the Move Segment arrows to make the two images congruent. The overlays were not aligned due to polar rotation of the head during the hour-long acquisition. It took me a while to figure that out.

There are some obvious artifacts, but in time I hope to master the art of superimposed comet processing.
Check it out for yourself at my New Images web page
http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm

I have a lot to learn about comet image superposition processing -- I'd appreciate advice on improving my images.

Clear skies,

Dennis Persyk
Hampshire, IL
Igloo (Now Roll-Off) Observatory Home Page http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk
New Images http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm
Pier Design http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/Pier_Design.htm
Daily Bread Inspirational Page http://users.foxvalley.net/~dpersyk/DailyBread/

Date:  Mon, 03 Oct 2011 09:25:11 +0200
From:  Gerald Rhemann 
Subject:  comet 45P
Hello everybody,

There have been a lot of great images posted on this group from this comet.
I personally imaged the comet two times.

In the first attempt at processing I run around gradients and really no
processing flow was efficient. All versions looked unnatural - dawn with
clouds cannot produce a smooth dark sky around thus I decided to let it be
like it is:

http://www.astrostudio.at/2_Bright%20Comets.php?img=images/2_Bright%20Comets
/113_45P.jpg

On this black and white Video one can see the changes in the comets tail
within the 12 minutes of expose time.


http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=V6gXdPdginU

Images captured this morning will follow soon.

Gerald

Date:  Fri, 07 Oct 2011 06:06:55 -0600
From:  Alan Hale 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: C/2010 X1
Hi everyone,

For whatever it's worth -- probably not much -- I made an unsuccessful
visual attempt this morning (Oct. 7.48 UT). The altitude was fairly low and
the zodiacal light fairly strong, but in any event, I couldn't see anything
even remotely convincing. I tried to see if there might be any kind of
diffuse "cloud," but still, nothing.

Sincerely,

Alan 

Date:  Fri, 07 Oct 2011 05:36:36 -0700
From:  kronk@cometography.com
Subject:  RE: [Comet-Images] Re: C/2010 X1
I was also unsuccessful this morning (October 7.42 UT), both visually
and photographically. The visual searches were made using 20x80
binoculars and my 33-cm reflector. The photographic search was made from
my observatory using an 80mm APO and a modified Canon T2i DSLR (FOV =
1.5 degrees), as well as my 20-cm LX200 and a B&W MallinCam Hyper video
camera (FOV = 20 arc minutes). The latter system was showing stars to
magnitude 16, but no indication of a cloud of debris.

Gary

Thanks....not knowing which of the two images in the animation is first and assuming
that the one with the arrow is the last image, I suspect that you may have capture a
remnant of this comet; the trajectory and degree of motion of your time frame is
correct for the projected ephemeris motion on Oct. 7 UT.

The faint possible moving fragment would then be south and west of the ephemeris
position by a slight amount.

Date:  Wed, 12 Oct 2011 19:41:23 +0200
From:  Juan José González Suárez 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: C/2010 X1
Three days ago, I posted a visual observation made on the last available
night without moonlight interference :

C/2010 X1 (Elenin):
2011 Oct. 9.20 UT: m1=10.7, Dia.=6', DC=1/,
Tail: 0.2 deg. in PA 310 deg, 20 cm SCT (77x).
[ The coma appears large and very diffuse,
without central condensation. Observation made from
mountain location under very good seeing conditions.
Nearby field stars checked in DSS. Zodiacal light.
Altitude: 23 deg.].

At this point, it is useful to provide additional information.

We are again speaking about one of these "problematic, extremely diluted
and fuzzy comets" ...

But for me this case wasn't problematic or near the threshold of
visual detection. It was a clear observation ( the atmospheric
conditions in the Cantabrian Mountains were near optimal down to the
line of horizon ) made in the course of a short observing session ( 1
hour approx. ) between moonset and the beginning of the morning
astronomical twilight. Under such very good conditions, and besides
C/2010 X1, my plan was to observe another four comets ( C/2010 G2,
C/2011 S2, 49P, and 45P at low altitude ), so I only could dedicate
approx. 10 min to the observation and magnitude estimate of C/2010 X1,
at low magnification as necessary. I didn't check for the motion, given
the short time-interval and the apparent lack of central condensation in
such a large ( 6' ) coma. The geometric center of this coma was close to
the MPC ephemeris position, with an error bar of +/- 4'.

Best regards and clear skies,

J. J. Gonzalez

( P.S.: as previously told, I don't like to discuss again on the
diversity among CCD and visual observations ... ).

------------------------------------------------------------

Date:  Wed, 12 Oct 2011 21:43:07 -0000
From:  dennis_persyk 
Subject:  Comet C/2009 P1 Cooled CCD and DSLR
Conditions were not favorable but I wanted to get some more experience with imaging with the Canon T1i DSLR and Starlight Xpress SXVR-H9 cooled CCD. The phase 0.49 moon was 43 degrees south of P1 and my Sky Quality Meter registered a moon glow of 17.8 mag/(sq arc sec). That corresponds to a NELM of about magnitude 3 -- pretty bright sky. The moon was by far the greatest source of light pollution that night.

Images, commentary, data and at the link below -- please take a look.

http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm .

Clear skies,

Dennis Persyk
Hampshire, IL
Igloo (Now Roll-Off) Observatory Home Page http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk
New Images http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/new.htm
Pier Design http://users.FoxValley.net/~dpersyk/Pier_Design.htm
Daily Bread Inspirational Page (Helicopter Parable) http://users.foxvalley.net/~dpersyk/DailyBread/ 

Date:  Thu, 13 Oct 2011 10:20:14 +1100
From:  Alan Watson 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: C/2010 X1
On Wed, Oct 12, 2011 at 7:19 PM, gvnn64@libero.it wrote:

>
> I have seen the object you are referring to in STEREO HI2A images.
> Can you determine how close it is to the MPC ephemerids?
>

Gidday Giovanni, Sorry I can't do all the maths necessary to determine
this.
This is how I work, I have STarry night pro-plus and use the comet data it
downloads from the MPEC guys.
The STEREO satellites behave like asteroids with circular orbits, so this
allows me to have them included into the asteroid data.
I can position the point of view in starry night to sit very close to each
STEREO satellite and look sun wards.
I make minor adjustments using the star fields in starry night. It is
generally very close to the STEREO FOV.
Here is a starry night movie of the current STEREOA HI2 FOV , zoomed in a
little. Elenin and 45P can be seen, they are in good position compared with
the actual FOV.
http://flic.kr/p/avknw1

I have used GRAS , but have a problem with PAYPAL, so not signed up at this
time. Not really wanting to tell you guys how to operate. I used the MPC
ephemerids generator at 15min steps, this usually let me get a comet in a
GRAS FOV. So perhaps a stepped set of images moving forward in the orbit may
detect it. It seems to be moving quite fast.

Kind regards, Alan Watson. 
Date:  Thu, 13 Oct 2011 10:51:28 +1030
From:  Ian Musgrave & Peta O'Donohue 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: C/2010 X1
G'Day All

You can use the Horizons email server to get the position of X1 as
seen from STEREO A, then compare the STEREO A images with the
Horizons ephemeris; Here's a example I used a while back for Encke,
make sure that the body of the email has no extraneous material (no
sigs etc.) Comet Elenin is just above the lower travel limit of the
GRAS scopes at astronomical twilight, so a systematic search with
narrow field instruments is going to be hard. I might try a long
exposure with the widefield instrument tonight. If the universe lets me.

send to : horizons@ssd.jpl.nasa.gov
Subject: JOB C/2009 02 Stereo A

!$$SOF
EMAIL_ADDR = ' '
COMMAND= 'C/2009 O2'
OBJ_DATA = 'YES'
MAKE_EPHEM = 'YES'
TABLE_TYPE = 'OBS'
CENTER = '500@stereo-a'
START_TIME = '2010-MARCH-27 8:09'
STOP_TIME = '2010-APRIL-25 8:09'
STEP_SIZE = '12 hours'
QUANTITIES = '1,2,9'
REF_SYSTEM = 'J2000'
CAL_FORMAT = 'CAL'
APPARENT = 'AIRLESS'
TIME_ZONE = '+09:30'
RANGE_UNITS = 'AU'
CSV_FORMAT = 'YES'
!$$EOF

Eh, I just did it, here's the STEREO A centric ephemeris for Elenin
for Oct 9, in the time steps of the STEREO imager.

*********************************************************************************************************
Date_(ZONE)_HR:MN, , ,R.A._(ICRF/J2000.0), DEC_(ICRF/J2000.0),
R.A._(a-app), DEC_(a-app), T-mag, N-mag,
*********************************************************************************************************
$$SOE
2011-Oct-09 00:09, , ,22 36 57.07,-07 32 09.8, 22 36 56.05,-07 32
15.6, 9.96, 15.25,
2011-Oct-09 02:09, , ,22 37 30.16,-07 28 43.0, 22 37 29.14,-07 28
48.8, 9.97, 15.26,
2011-Oct-09 04:09, , ,22 38 03.20,-07 25 16.3, 22 38 02.18,-07 25
22.1, 9.98, 15.26,
2011-Oct-09 06:09, , ,22 38 36.19,-07 21 49.7, 22 38 35.17,-07 21

At 09:50 AM 13/10/2011, you wrote:

>On Wed, Oct 12, 2011 at 7:19 PM,
>gvnn64@libero.it
><gvnn64@libero.it> wrote:
>
>I have seen the object you are referring to in STEREO HI2A images.
>Can you determine how close it is to the MPC ephemerids?
>
> Gidday Giovanni, Sorry I can't do all the maths necessary to determine this.
>This is how I work, I have STarry night pro-plus and use the comet
>data it downloads from the MPEC guys.
>The STEREO satellites behave like asteroids with circular orbits, so
>this allows me to have them included into the asteroid data.
>I can position the point of view in starry night to sit very close
>to each STEREO satellite and look sun wards.
>I make minor adjustments using the star fields in starry night. It
>is generally very close to the STEREO FOV.
>Here is a starry night movie of the current STEREOA HI2 FOV , zoomed
>in a little. Elenin and 45P can be seen, they are in good position
>compared with the actual FOV.
> http://flic.kr/p/avknw1
>
>I have used GRAS , but have a problem with PAYPAL, so not signed up
>at this time. Not really wanting to tell you guys how to operate. I
>used the MPC ephemerids generator at 15min steps, this usually let
>me get a comet in a GRAS FOV. So perhaps a stepped set of images
>moving forward in the orbit may detect it. It seems to be moving quite fast.
>
>Kind regards, Alan Watson.
>

> >
> > I have seen the object you are referring to in STEREO HI2A images.
> > Can you determine how close it is to the MPC ephemerids?
> >
>
> Gidday Giovanni, Sorry I can't do all the maths necessary to determine
> this.
> This is how I work, I have STarry night pro-plus and use the comet data it
> downloads from the MPEC guys.
> The STEREO satellites behave like asteroids with circular orbits, so this
> allows me to have them included into the asteroid data.
> I can position the point of view in starry night to sit very close to each
> STEREO satellite and look sun wards.
> I make minor adjustments using the star fields in starry night. It is
> generally very close to the STEREO FOV.
> Here is a starry night movie of the current STEREOA HI2 FOV , zoomed in a
> little. Elenin and 45P can be seen, they are in good position compared with
> the actual FOV.
> http://flic.kr/p/avknw1
>
> I have used GRAS , but have a problem with PAYPAL, so not signed up at this
> time. Not really wanting to tell you guys how to operate. I used the MPC
> ephemerids generator at 15min steps, this usually let me get a comet in a
> GRAS FOV. So perhaps a stepped set of images moving forward in the orbit may
> detect it. It seems to be moving quite fast.
>
> Kind regards, Alan Watson.
>

min, therefore poses unit 120s I should have a net instead of a
quasi-off point ...?!

Date:  Tue, 18 Oct 2011 15:23:46 +0200
From:  Bernd Häusler 
Subject:  C/2008 S3 (Boattini) on October, 18 2011
Hi,
the comet passed the Perihelion on June, 8 2011 in 8.02 AU distance to the
Sun.
A tail is still visible, 19" in PA256.
The comet's actual distance to the Sun is 8.05AU

http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/c2008s3_20111018.htm

overview with three observations since 2009:
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/c2008s3.htm

Orbit Diagram: http://ssd.jpl.nasa.gov/sbdb.cgi?orb=1;sstr=2008+S3

Clear skies
Bernhard Haeusler
B82 Maidbronn
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/index.htm

Date:  Mon, 24 Oct 2011 13:40:00 +0000
From:  Albert van Duin 
Subject:  Elenin dust trail?
Last night I made 3 - 300s images at the location of 2010X1 Elenin with
my 40cm F/4 Newtonian.
Time: 2011-10-24T00:26:32 UT - 2011-10-24T00:41:57 UT

http://astropix.nl/web/EleninCombineFilesAdpAdd3x300secneg.jpg

The corners look weird because my filters are a bit too small, but I
think the flatfielding and calibration is OK.
There seems to be a faint band of dust vertically in the image, North is
left, the comet position should be about bottom right.
The 40' x 30' field is a bit too small to catch the whole cloud...

http://astropix.nl/web/EleninCombineFilesAdpAdd3x300sec.jpg shows the
positive image, at the top there seems to be some faint haze.

Regards,
Albert van Duin

From:  Bernd Häusler 
Subject:  image of C/2008 FK75 on October, 28 2011  and faint nebula
Hi and hola,
the faint comet passed an unknown faint nebula (HII region?).
The nebula is real (also present in POSS II images), but I couldn't find the
name of the object. It is not mentioned in the Sharpless catalogue of HII
regions. Also no detection in NED or Aladin. But perhaps I am too silly to
perform the correct query search.

Maybe Seiichi or any other of you can help to find the nebula's name,
please.

See all images under:
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/c2008fk75_20111028.htm
overview:
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/c2008fk75.htm

From:  Bernd Häusler 
Subject:  AW: [Comet-Images] image of C/2008 FK75 on October, 28 2011 and faint nebula
Dear Bob,
thanks a lot for your help.
Meanwhile I loaded an DSS image of the POSS II with a field of view of one
degree.
This wide-field image is showing a large nebulous structure which obviously
belongs to a huge nebuly of the Milky Way.
On the image of comet Lemmon-Siding Spring we can see the most Eastern edge
of the nebula.
Have a look to the following link, please, which shows the large nebula
field.
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/c2008fk75_20111028_poss.htm
See you and clear skies
Bernhard

Hi and hola,
the faint comet passed an unknown faint nebula (HII region?).
The nebula is real (also present in POSS II images), but I couldn't find the
name of the object. It is not mentioned in the Sharpless catalogue of HII
regions. Also no detection in NED or Aladin. But perhaps I am too silly to
perform the correct query search.

Maybe Seiichi or any other of you can help to find the nebula's name,
please.

Subject:  C/2010 X1 Elenin near Simeis 147 on November 1, 2011
Hi all,

The comet was in dust-rich area near Simeis 147.
http://www.flickr.com/photos/hiroc/6311486987/
A bright star is near the comet.
The small plus marks indicate the predicted position
at the start and the end of 8 times 15 minute-exposure.
Some asteroids were also in the frame and identified.

hiro in Tokyo

Date:  Sun, 27 Nov 2011 15:34:13 +0100
From:  Bernd Häusler 
Subject:  observation of unusual object 2011 UF305 in November 2011
Hello,
after four sessions of observation, the object is showing still no cometary
action.
With a period of around 9200 years and an actual distance of 3.96 AU from
Earth, (3.41 AU from Sun), the object is like a typical asteroid on my ccd
images, starlike but softer than a star.
More informations on :
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/2011uf305.htm
Bernhard Haeusler
B82 Maidbronn

Date:  Sat, 03 Dec 2011 08:21:37 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Astrometry and image of TLc001
Hi,

I got some astrometry on TLc001 for nearly two hours this morning (2011 Dec 2.52-60) with a 35cm ACF SCT and SBIG STL11000M CCD. I took 30 second unguided images through a clear filter. The comet was very low in the southeast – never getting above about 20 degrees in altitude. The astrometry report is below – as is a stacked image using 60 x 30s images...

The comet appears to moving at roughly 8’/hour in a PA of about 77* (roughly ENE at about 3.2 degrees a day). On individual images it looks to be about 40 arcseconds in diameter with a DC of about 3. There is a slight condensation at the centre.

Astrometry -
COD E94
CON John Drummond, 23 Bilham Road, Patutahi, Gisborne [john_drummond@xtra.co.nz]
OBS J. Drummond
MEA J. Drummond
TEL 0.35-m f/10 Schmidt-Cassegrain + CCD
ACK MPCReport file updated 2011.12.03 07:02:28

Date:  Sun, 04 Dec 2011 11:40:47 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet 2011 W3 (Lovejoy) imaged this morning - 2011 Dec 03 UT
Hi all,

I imaged newly discovered C/2011W3 (Lovejoy) this morning with a 35cm f10 Meade SCT and SBIG STL11000M CCD. 38 x 30 second sublights, 2x2 binning. The stars have been obliterated from high cloud and stacking on the comet.

Here’s a link to the image (also attached for some people) -

http://groups.yahoo.com/group/Comet-Images/photos/album/1986578311/pic/547612517/view?picmode=large&mode=tn&order=ordinal&start=1&dir=asc
or
http://tinyurl.com/7f37oea

Astrometry has been done on the images and sent in.

John Drummond

International Astro Union Code: E94

Subject:  Comet Lovejoy
I'm wondering, in SOHO LASCO C3 image 2011/12/16 06:30, what caused the bright object that appears about the 10 o'clock position next to the occulting disc. It seems to have the spike you see from bright objects like planets when they overload the CCD, but it only appears in one image since it's so close the the disc.

Date:  Sat, 24 Dec 2011 05:39:00 +1100
From:  David Nicholls 
Subject:  Comet Lovejoy from Canberra - finally!
The first clear morning in Canberra since perihelion. This photo taken atop Red Hill in the middle of Canberra.

Camera: Canon 5D2, 50mm f/1.8II at f/2, 1.6 seconds at ISO 3200, 4:10am, about 10 minutes after the start of astronomical twilight.

http://www.dcnicholls.com/misc/lovejoy-0059.jpg

The comet is like a faint version of Ikeya-Seki - close to the same size though much fainter. But a lovely sight in the predawn sky, and worth the wait!

DN 
Date:  Fri, 23 Dec 2011 11:16:30 -0800

Date:  Mon, 26 Dec 2011 22:01:17 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet Lovejoy this morning - 2011 December 25 UT
Hi all,

my observing mate John Burt and I hit Young Nicks Head this morning. I got some patchy glimpses of Lovejoy from Whakatane (thanks Keith and Norm) on the morning of the 24th December but nothing like this morning (26th Dec 2011) from Gisborne, New Zealand. Wow, what a cool comet! The tail extended for 27 degrees and was about 3 degrees wide at the widest – up near the end. No head visible – jut a big tail in the sky. Lovejoy was easy to see with the naked eye – indeed, 45 minutes into astronomical twilight all the Milky Way at the same altitude and higher had long disappeared but Lovejoy’s tail was still visible against the bluish sky.

Attached in an image (more to come later) of John Burt modelling – I would have preferred a bikini-clad female holding the binoculars, but you use what you’ve got! Image details in the file name...
http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_Lovejoy-2011w3-20mm_f2,8-12800iso-28sec-2011dec26-3,11am-drummond.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/74ueth3

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory Complex
International Astro Union Code: E94
Gisborne, New Zealand
E: 177d 53', S: 38d 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm

Date:  Tue, 27 Dec 2011 20:02:23 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet Lovejoy's 38 degree tail
Hi,

this morning (2011 Dec 26, 15hrs UT) I imaged what I thought was beyond the end of Comet Lovejoy’s tail with a 70mm Sigma lens at f2.8 and with a Canon 500D DSLR. I combined four x two minute exposures (piggybacked). For orientation, b-g Crux are at the upper right, b Centauri is at lower right, e Cen is at mid-lower left. The tail is the faint, greenish hue starting at the bottom and going straight up to nearly the top – in my reckoning a tail length of 38 degrees!

http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/Tail_tip_crux-70mm_sigma_lens-f2,8-4x2min-111227-4am_NZST-drummond.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/78jp3nj

Cheers

John Drummond

Date:  Wed, 28 Dec 2011 11:19:06 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet Lovejoy this morning - 2011 December 27, 1400 hrs UT
Hi,

John Burt came out to my place (Patutahi, Gisborne, New Zealand) this morning and we piggybacked our cameras on the 16” equatorial. Canon 500D DSLR, 20mm Canon lens at f2.8, 3 x 2 minute exposures @ 800 ISO taken on 2011 December 27, 1400 hrs UT. The image can be seen at -

http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/Comet_Lovejoy-2011w3-20mm_canon_lens@f2,8-800iso-3x2min-111228-drummond-web-cropped.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/7srmaph

One thing we both noticed visually (and would like confirmed) is that a section of tail about 2.5 – 3 degrees from the head was much brighter than the rest of the comet and tail. It is about 8 degrees long and 1 degree wide. It really stood out due to it’s brightness. We wondered if the head that seems to be a line of material within the comet has spread out and replenished the section of tail we saw... However, the photo shows a line of cloud? over that section – if this were then that section of tail should be fainter, correct?

Can anyone confirm this brightening in this section of tail?

Cheers

John Drummond

Subject:  images of new comet C/2011 UF305 B82 Maidbronn
Hi,
you can find images of five observation nights since November 2011 here:

http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/2011uf305.htm

The object looked like an normal asteroid on all my images without any
cometary feature. The unusual orbital elements reminded from beginning on,
that the object has a cometarian nature.

Clear skies
Bernhard Haeusler
B82 Maidbronn
http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/index.htm 

Date:  Fri, 30 Dec 2011 20:25:51 +0100
From:  Gerald Rhemann 
Subject:  comet c/2009P1 Garradd
Hello everybody,

This is an image of comet Garradd growing up in the morning sky. The image
was taken yesterday morning under very awkward conditions. I gone along with
Michael to one of his observing places  anyway the comet was not as bright
and tail is not as long as at the images I´d taken at dusk in November. The
bright yellow star is Lambda Hercules 4.4 mag.:

http://www.astrostudio.at/2_Bright%20Comets.php?img=images/2_Bright%20Comets
/121_garradd_dec29.jpg

I wish you a Happy New Year!

Best regards

Gerald

Love to see your images posted here Gerald. You and Michael do great work. If I can ask, do you and Michael live close enough to get together or do you communicate the images over the web? Sorry to ask a question I could spend time researching locations but you guys have been working together a long time and I am sure would make a good article for a magazine. Happy New Year and all the best to you, Michael and all the members of the board. Let me add that after two great comets in the southern skys I am looking to a good show in 2013 with the reminder by Kelly Beatty of the up coming comet C/2011 L4. If I have to stand on my head for the next 15 months for a good show I will, BUT considering it will not cross the orbit of Jupiter untill March 2012 and not reach northern skys untill March 2013------I would rather not.
Mike H.

Date:  Sat, 31 Dec 2011 15:26:49 +0100
From:  Gerald Rhemann 
Subject:  AW: [Comet-Images] Re: comet c/2009P1 Garradd
Hello Mike,

Thank you for your nice words. I frequently stay in contact with Michael and
sometimes, when I find time I ask him to go with him for imaging. Many years
ago we had much more communication and shared a lot of observations. We live
very close and the distance to the different observing places is 1-2 hours.
Anyway  I´m ever impressed by the experience and professional work of
Michael and I enjoy the discussions during the stays. I will talk about an
article for a magazine like Sky& Tel with Michael J

Gerald
